The Story of the Apple (Timber Press, Portland, Oregon, USA, 2006)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d39870e3991">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Korban, S.S. &amp; Skirvin, R.M. Nomenclature of the cultivate apple. HortScience 19, 177–180 (1984)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d39870e3994">46</a></sup>.</p><p>A practical goal of sequencing the complex heterozygous apple genome is to accelerate the breeding of this economically important perennial crop species. Many genes related to disease resistance, aroma and taste, plant development and reaction to the environment have been identified and mapped to the chromosomes. In addition, SNP molecular markers have been made available at a frequency of 4.4 SNPs per kb. These markers are currently being used in advanced breeding programs and comparative genetic studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Celton, J.M., Tustin, D.S., Chagne, D. &amp; Gardiner, S.E. Construction of a dense genetic linkage map for apple rootstocks using SSRs developed from Malus ESTs and Pyrus genomic sequences. Tree Genet. Genomes 5, 93–107 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4001">31</a></sup> that should speed cultivar development. The anchored sequence of the apple genome will be a tool to initiate a new era in the breeding of this crop. The availability of nearly all apple gene sequences should benefit apple researchers by enabling genome-wide functional studies and accelerating establishment of gene-trait relationships.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">URLs.</h3><p><i>Arabidposis thaliana</i> (TAIR Release 8.0), <a href="ftp://ftp.arabidopsis.org">ftp://ftp.arabidopsis.org</a>; <i>Carica papaya</i>, <a href="ftp://asgpb.mhpcc.hawaii.edu/papaya/annotation/">ftp://asgpb.mhpcc.hawaii.edu/papaya/annotation/</a>; <i>Populus trichocarpa</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v1.1.), <a href="http://genome.jgi-psf.org/Poptr1_1/Poptr1_1.home.html">http://genome.jgi-psf.org/Poptr1_1/Poptr1_1.home.html</a>; <i>Vitis vinifera</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v2.0), <a href="http://genomics.research.iasma.it">http://genomics.research.iasma.it</a>; <i>Oryza sativa</i> (MSU Rice Genome Annotation Project Release 6.0 assembly), <a href="http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/index.shtml">http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/index.shtml</a>; <i>Sorghum bicolor</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v1.4), <a href="http://www.phytozome.net/sorghum">http://www.phytozome.net/sorghum</a>; <i>Cucumis sativus</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v1.0), <a href="http://cucumber.genomics.org.cn/page/cucumber/index.jsp">http://cucumber.genomics.org.cn/page/cucumber/index.jsp</a>; <i>Glycine max</i> (assembly release Glyma1, annotation Glyma1.0), <a href="http://genome.jgi-psf.org/soybean/soybean.home.html">http://genome.jgi-psf.org/soybean/soybean.home.html</a>; <i>Zea mays</i> (assembly release B73 RefGen_v1), <a href="http://www.maizesequence.org/Zea_mays/Info/Index">http://www.maizesequence.org/Zea_mays/Info/Index</a>; <i>Brachypodium distachyon</i> (assembly release v1.0, annotation v1.0), <a href="http://www.brachybase.org">http://www.brachybase.org</a>; integrated genetic map, <a href="http://genomics.research.iasma.it">http://genomics.research.iasma.it</a>; RepBase14.01, <a href="http://www.girinst.org">http://www.girinst.org</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec9" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10">Plant material.</h3><p>The DNA of <i>Malus</i> × <i>domestica</i>, variety 'Golden Delicious', was extracted from young leaves of a two-year-old plant grown in the greenhouse at Fondazione Edmund Mac–Istituto Agrario di San Michele all'Adige. The dihaploid 'Golden Delicious' derivative genotype used at Washington State University and the University of Washington to produce 1.5× of 454 sequence was developed by the French National Institute for Agricultural Research<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Lespinasse, Y., Bouvier, L., Djulbic, M. &amp; Chevreau, E. Haploidy in apple and pear. Acta Hortic. 538, 49–54 (1999)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4147">47</a></sup> after a spontaneous duplication of a haploid individual selected in the progeny of a selfed derivative from 'Golden Delicious'<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Lespinasse, Y., Bouvier, L., Djulbic, M. &amp; Chevreau, E. Haploidy in apple and pear. Acta Hortic. 538, 49–54 (1999)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4151">47</a></sup>.</p><p>'Golden Delicious' was chosen for genome sequencing because of its extensive use in apple breeding programs worldwide. Its heterozygous status did not hamper the genome assembly, thanks to expertise gained in heterozygous grape sequencing<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Zharkikh, A. et al. Sequencing and assembly of highly heterozygous genome of Vitis vinifera L. cv Pinot Noir: problems and solutions. J. Biotechnol. 136, 38–43 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4158">1</a></sup>. Indeed, it allowed the inference of both haplotypes, thus giving access to both allelic versions for further genomic projects, and the development of SNP markers. The dihaploid genotype was important for a more accurate haplotype phase determination.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11">Bacterial artificial chromosomes, shotgun libraries and Sanger sequencing.</h3><p>The apple bacterial artificial chromosome (BAC) library was from high–molecular weight genomic DNA (Amplicon Express), prepared as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Tao, Q., Wang, A. &amp; Zhang, H.B. One large-insert plant-transformation-competent BIBAC library and three BAC libraries of Japonica rice for genome research in rice and other grasses. Theor. Appl. Genet. 105, 1058–1066 (2002)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4170">48</a></sup>. The fosmid and shotgun libraries were from genomic DNA provided by R. Meilan (Oregon State University). The shotgun libraries were from DNA sheared with a Gene Machines Hydroshear device. The DNA was size-selected for inserts from 2 to 12 kb to produce libraries of 2, 3, 6, 9 and 11 kb (average sizes). DNA was amplified with the Templiphi kit (GE Healthcare) and sequenced with the Sanger method.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Libraries and 454 pyrosequencing.</h3><p>Two random shotgun genomic libraries were created by fragmentation of 10 μg of genomic DNA with the GS FLX Titanium library preparation kit (454 Life Sciences). Sequencing was performed with the GS FLX instrument (454 Life Sciences). Further details on library construction and pyrosequencing are in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.654#MOESM4">Supplementary Note</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Genome assembly and anchoring.</h3><p>From 27 libraries, 39.2 million reads (11.6 billion Q20 bases) were produced by Sanger sequencing and sequencing by synthesis (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.654#MOESM4">Supplementary Table 1</a>). Chloroplast and mitochondrial sequences were identified with 847× and 168× coverage, respectively. Chloroplast (160,068 bp) and mitochondrial (396,947 bp) genomes were used to assess sequence quality and clone size in each library. Preliminary estimates of one to two SNPs per 1,000 bp were adopted in the assembly process. The actual SNP rate (4.4 SNPs per 1,000 bp) indicates that the preliminary value was conservative. Metacontigs were constructed on the basis of paired reads matching to nonrepetitive parts of contigs. Merging of contigs into metacontigs accepted a maximum total average coverage of 20×. Fifteen BAC clones were sequenced and individually assembled for quality assessment of sequencing accuracy and genome assembly.</p><p>Genetic maps used in metacontig anchoring were derived from six F<sub>1</sub> populations totaling 720 individuals (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.654#MOESM4">Supplementary Note</a>). Simple sequence repeat primer sequences<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Guilford, P. et al. Microsatellites in Malus X domestica (apple): abundance, polymorphism and cultivar identification. Theor. Appl. Genet. 94, 249–254 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4204">49</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Liebhard, R. et al. Development and characterisation of 140 new microsatellites in apple (Malus x domestica Borkh.). Mol. Breed. 10, 217–241 (2002)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4207">50</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Gianfranceschi, L., Seglias, N., Tarchini, R., Komjanc, M. &amp; Gessler, C. Simple sequence repeats for the genetic analysis of apple. Theor. Appl. Genet. 96, 1069–1076 (1998)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4210">51</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Silfverberg-Dilworth, E. et al. Microsatellite markers spanning the apple (Malus x domestica Borkh.) genome. Tree Genet. Genomes 2, 202–224 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4213">52</a></sup> enabled detection of 196 polymorphic markers. Thirty-four SNP-based markers were from apple EST sequences, and 1,489 from genomic electronic SNPs, deduced by genomic sequence comparison between the two haplotypes present in the heterozygous genotype of 'Golden Delicious'. The consensus genetic maps for the six populations were used to generate an integrated genetic map (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/ng.654#MOESM4">Supplementary Fig. 1</a>) with TMAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Cartwright, D.A., Troggio, M., Velasco, R. &amp; Gutin, A. Genetic mapping in the presence of genotyping errors. Genetics 176, 2521–2527 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4220">53</a></sup> and a minimum logarithmic odds of 10.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Repetitive elements.</h3><p>The highest-coverage sequences were characterized as repetitive elements. Identified elements were iteratively masked, and the remaining sequences were searched for the next highest–coverage sequence. For each type, members were searched (BLASTN and BLASTX) against RepBase14.01, the NCBI databases and the Uniprot database<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Uniprot Consortium. The universal protein resource (UniProt). Nucleic Acids Res. 36, D190–D195 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4233">54</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Wicker, T. et al. A unified classification system for eukaryotic transposable elements. Nat. Rev. Genet. 8, 973–982 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4236">55</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Gene prediction and annotation.</h3><p>FgenesH<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Solovyev, V., Kosarev, P., Seledsov, I. &amp; Vorobyev, D. Automatic annotation of eukaryotic genes, pseudogenes and promoters. Genome Biol. 7, S10 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4248">56</a></sup>, Twinscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Korf, I., Flicek, P., Duan, D. &amp; Brent, M.R. Integrating genomic homology into gene structure prediction. Bioinformatics 17, S140–S148 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4252">57</a></sup>, GlimmerHMM<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Majoros, W.H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S.L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878–2879 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4256">58</a></sup> and GeneWise<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988–995 (2004)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4260">59</a></sup> were used. The predicted protein sequences were searched with BLAST against Uniprot, protein domain data banks and plant protein databases annotated with GO terms. The GO terms were extracted by Argot<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Fontana, P., Cestaro, A., Velasco, R., Formentin, E. &amp; Toppo, S. Rapid annotation of anonymous sequences from genome projects using semantic similarities and a weighting scheme in gene ontology. PLoS ONE 4, e4619 (2009)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4264">60</a></sup> and InterproScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Mulder, N. &amp; Apweiler, R. InterPro and InterProScan—Tools for protein sequence classification and comparison. Methods Mol. Biol. 396, 59–70 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4269">61</a></sup>. Unique genes were searched against proteins from rice, poplar, papaya, barrel medic, sorghum, <i>Arabidopsis</i> and grape by BLAST with an <i>e</i>-value cutoff of <i>e</i><sup>−10</sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">All-versus-all BLAST.</h3><p>Protein sequences from apple, poplar<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Tuskan, G.A. et al. The genome of black cottonwood, Populus trichocarpa (Torr. &amp; Gray). Science 313, 1596–1604 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4291">6</a></sup> and grape<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Velasco, R. et al. A high quality draft consensus sequence of the genome of a heterozygous grapevine variety. PLoS ONE 2, e1326 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4295">2</a></sup> were extracted from a BLAST database, and pairwise similarities between all genes was obtained by BLASTP <i>e</i>-value (cutoff <i>e</i><sup>−5</sup>; 500 hits)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Altschul, S.F. et al. Gapped BLAST and PSI-BLAST: a new generation of protein database search programs. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 3389–3402 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4306">62</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Gene families.</h3><p>Tribe-MCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Enright, A.J., Van Dongen, S. &amp; Ouzounis, C.A. An efficient algorithm for large-scale detection of protein families. Nucleic Acids Res. 30, 1575–1584 (2002)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4318">63</a></sup> was adopted, with parameter <i>I</i> set to 2 and parameter 'scheme' to 4; other parameters were at default values.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Detection of collinearity.</h3><p>Metacontig anchoring generated lists of apple genes, from which transposable element–related sequences were removed. Poplar and grape gene lists were as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Velasco, R. et al. A high quality draft consensus sequence of the genome of a heterozygous grapevine variety. PLoS ONE 2, e1326 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4333">2</a></sup>. Colinearity in the gene order was detected with i-ADHoRe 2.4 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Simillion, C., Janssens, K., Sterck, L. &amp; Van de Peer, Y. i-ADHoRe 2.0: an improved tool to detect degenerated genomic homology using genomic profiles. Bioinformatics 24, 127–128 (2008)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4336">64</a>), with the following parameters: family blast type; alignment method, gg; gap size, 30; cluster gap, 35; <i>q</i> value, 0.9; prob cutoff, 0.0001; anchor points, 4; level 2 only, false.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19"><i>K</i><sub>s</sub> dating.</h3><p>Homologous genes were aligned with CLUSTALW<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Thompson, J.D., Higgins, D.G. &amp; Gibson, T.J. CLUSTAL W: improving the sensitivity of progressive multiple sequence alignment through sequence weighting, position-specific gap penalties and weight matrix choice. Nucleic Acids Res. 22, 4673–4680 (1994)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4355">65</a></sup>. <i>K</i><sub>s</sub> dating was based on codeml<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Yang, Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput. Appl. Biosci. 13, 555–556 (1997)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4363">66</a></sup> with the following parameters: verbose, 0; noisy, 0; runmode, −2; seqtype, 1; model, 0; NSsites, 0; icode, 0; fix_alpha, 0; fix_kappa, 0; RateAncestor, 0.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Molecular distances, taxonomy and phylogeny.</h3><p>Molecular distances were analyzed with EST data sets. A two-way alignment between apple and pear contigs (cDNA sequences, data not shown ) was first generated. Sequences from apple and pear were combined with the peach sequence (EST databases) in three-way alignments. Phylogenetic analysis of the <i>Wx</i> genes included <i>gbss1</i> (<i>Wx1</i>) and <i>gbss2</i> (<i>Wx2</i>) sequences from the apple genome and from ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Potter, D. et al. Phylogeny and classification of Rosaceae. Plant Syst. Evol. 266, 5–43 (2007)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4391">12</a>. Sequences were aligned by T-coffee<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Notredame, C., Higgins, D.G. &amp; Heringa, J. T-Coffee: a novel method for fast and accurate multiple sequence alignment. J. Mol. Biol. 302, 205–217 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4395">67</a></sup>, and phylogenesis was by a Bayesian inference approach (MrBayes program). Phylogeny of Rosaceae was based on four chloroplast DNA sequences and on the nuclear internal transcribed spacer region. The data set included 6,308 positions in 85 operational taxonomic units, each representing one genus, aligned by a Bayesian method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Huelsenbeck, J.P. &amp; Ronquist, F. MRBAYES: Bayesian inference of phylogenetic trees. Bioinformatics 17, 754–755 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4399">68</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Apple domestication.</h3><p>A set of 74 <i>Malus</i> accessions, including 12 accessions of <i>M.</i> × <i>domestica</i> cultivars<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Noiton, D.A.M. &amp; Alspach, P.A. Founding clones, inbreeding, coancestry, and status number of modern apple cultivars. J. Am. Soc. Hortic. Sci. 121, 773–782 (1996)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4420">15</a></sup>, 10 of <i>M. sieversii</i> and 21 of <i>M. sylvestris</i>, was assembled. This included 31 of 34 recognized <i>Malus</i> species<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Janick, J., Cummins, J.N., Brown, S.K. &amp; Hemmat, M. Apples. in Fruit Breeding Vol. 1 (eds. Janick, J., Moore, J.J.) 1–77 (Wiley, New York, 1996)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4434">69</a></sup>. Twenty-three genes were resequenced and, after alignment<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Notredame, C., Higgins, D.G. &amp; Heringa, J. T-Coffee: a novel method for fast and accurate multiple sequence alignment. J. Mol. Biol. 302, 205–217 (2000)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4438">67</a></sup>, a concatenated 11,300-bp multilocus sequence was generated for each accession. Genetic relationships analysis used Splits-Tree v4.10 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Huson, D.H. &amp; Bryant, D. Application of phylogenetic networks in evolutionary studies. Mol. Biol. Evol. 23, 254–267 (2006)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4441">16</a>) and Hamming distance per pair of accessions. Haplotypes were computed with Phase v2.1 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Stephens, M., Smith, N.J. &amp; Donnelly, P. A new statistical method for haplotype reconstruction from population data. Am. J. Hum. Genet. 68, 978–989 (2001)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4444">70</a>). Nucleotide diversity (<i>π</i>), <i>H</i><sub>e</sub>, <i>H</i><sub>o</sub> and <i>F</i><sub>st</sub> values<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Wright, S. Evolution and the Genetics of Populations Vol. 4 (University of Chicago Press, 1978)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4465">17</a></sup> were computed with Arlequin 3.1 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Excoffier, L., Laval, G. &amp; Schneider, S. Arlequin (version 3.0): an integrated software package for population genetics data analysis. Evol. Bioinform. Online 1, 47–50 (2005)." href="/articles/ng.654#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d39870e4468">71</a>).</p></div></div></section>
